  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_90966565-7fcd-4463-a8ff-463ff6f75e27'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer4062992725214003989">Weaver, a young man who longs for a different life, is forced to flee his refugee settlement when everyone in it is massacred. In his flight for safety, Weaver stumbles upon a refuge of survivors hidden among the remains of a ruined city once known as Toronto.<br/> <br/>In the midst of building a new life, Weaver discovers he can do something strange: cast dreams into reality. Convi</span>
  <span id="freeText4062992725214003989" style="display:none">Weaver, a young man who longs for a different life, is forced to flee his refugee settlement when everyone in it is massacred. In his flight for safety, Weaver stumbles upon a refuge of survivors hidden among the remains of a ruined city once known as Toronto.<br /> <br />In the midst of building a new life, Weaver discovers he can do something strange: cast dreams into reality. Convinced it’s just an anomaly, he ignores it. That is until he learns of the mysterious man who waged war against his world — a man who calls himself the Dream Eater and harnesses the ability to animate nightmares into existence. The peaceful life Weaver hoped for begins to unravel when those of his new home are besieged by the Dream Eater and their lives placed in jeopardy. Weaver must learn to master his accursed ability before his new home is eradicated by the Dream Eater and human existence is pushed to the brink of extinction.</span>

<div id="review_438004538" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/438004538" />
    <a title=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/703854-rebecca"><img alt=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529467844p2/703854.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/438004538?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" href="/user/show/703854-rebecca"> ♥ Rebecca ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/16077831-dream-caster">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=own-ebook">own-ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=arcs-giveaways">arcs-giveaways</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer438004538" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5760875213181660974">This book's best feature is easily the original story idea and unique combo of genres. It is in a post-apocalyptic setting, set in Toronto, Canada, approximately 60 years after a cataclysmic war. But despite the futuristic setting, and even before taking Weaver's powers into consideration, it felt like a fantasy in theme, characters, and adventure. With the mysterious, seemingly all-powerful villain, who will likely remain faceless till the end of the series (which is fine, as long as he isnt We</span>
  <span id="freeText5760875213181660974" style="display:none">This book's best feature is easily the original story idea and unique combo of genres. It is in a post-apocalyptic setting, set in Toronto, Canada, approximately 60 years after a cataclysmic war. But despite the futuristic setting, and even before taking Weaver's powers into consideration, it felt like a fantasy in theme, characters, and adventure. With the mysterious, seemingly all-powerful villain, who will likely remain faceless till the end of the series (which is fine, as long as he isnt Weaver's father :P); the boy hero who discovers that he has a power that is the last hope. And Weaver and his friends seem to all have a sense of duty and self-sacrifice in protecting the Shield, which is common in classic fantasy. I am not surprised to see in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6552431.Najeev_Raj_Nadarajah" title="Najeev Raj Nadarajah" rel="nofollow noopener">Najeev Raj Nadarajah</a>'s bio that he was inspired by many famous fantasy authors. But this was its own unique new world. Apocalypse by design, where dreams come to life, and fire ignites creatures of nightmare. <br /><br />The writing style in this was extremely descriptive and had some beautiful imagery. I really enjoyed it for the most part. But sometimes it seemed a bit beyond YA, and a bit word-heavy. And the characters didnt talk like normal 16-18 year olds. It was too formal to seem natural. And some of the characters didnt have enough distinguishing characteristics to tell them apart. Most of them didnt stand out, and I kept mixing them up, despite remembering their names. <br /><br />But Weaver was a great hero, with great potential. He accomplished much already, with the little knowledge of his power that he has. I cant wait to see what he will accomplish in the future. And I hope to see Toggen there in that future too. I had no problem remembering Toggen. He was a great character, and a great friend, despite denying wanting any friends. He was so loyal and noble, and stoic. Haha, great combo. I cant wait to see what he is capable of either. Considering what faces them in the Dream Eater, they have far to go and much more to do before they are safe and it could be totally epic. I hope it is. I look forward to finding out.<br /><br /><i>I would like to thank the author for sending me a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5760875213181660974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_437359325" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/437359325" />
    <a title="Meera Nair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5221844-meera-nair"><img alt="Meera Nair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485068782p2/5221844.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/437359325?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meera Nair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meera Nair" href="/user/show/5221844-meera-nair">Meera Nair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer437359325" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14339452748246652863">Wow! :O <br/><br/>Dream Caster is a novel based on post-war Toronto. It explores the lives of a lucky few who managed to survive the catastrophe, which wipes mankind off the face of the Earth. Weaver, the protagonist, is a very soft and kind hearted character. He is left helpless as his world - the settlement where he grew up - collapses before his eyes. Ever since, thoughts of the disastrous event flood his mind, not allowing him any sense of peace. Soon, he discovers an absurd ability that he possesses </span>
  <span id="freeText14339452748246652863" style="display:none">Wow! :O <br /><br />Dream Caster is a novel based on post-war Toronto. It explores the lives of a lucky few who managed to survive the catastrophe, which wipes mankind off the face of the Earth. Weaver, the protagonist, is a very soft and kind hearted character. He is left helpless as his world - the settlement where he grew up - collapses before his eyes. Ever since, thoughts of the disastrous event flood his mind, not allowing him any sense of peace. Soon, he discovers an absurd ability that he possesses – the power to make his dreams come true! Now who doesn’t want that?! However with power comes responsibility and Weaver must learn to control it in time (and use it against the wrongdoers) in order to prevent extinction of life on this planet. <br /> <br />I would like to congratulate Najeev Nadarajah for a job well done and I hope this book crosses boundaries of success!! The storyline was out-of-the-world amazing. There were many jaw-dropping instances. I especially liked Weavers character! It has been inked beautifully with minor flaws as seen in every individual. I ABSOLUTELY loved the style of writing adopted by the author. I have never read a book with such a writing technique, before, and I can tell you, I am definitely hooked onto it. The anticipation with the oncoming 21st December 2012, makes the publishing date of the book (19th December) a little too apt. The book had such a huge impact, I was staring at the last page for awhile before I could snap out of the reverie. It was a lot to process at first but once everything started to seep in, it was mind blowing.Can’t wait for the 2nd book!! :D I recommend this book to anyone and everyone. There's something in it for all fiction lovers. :) <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14339452748246652863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer438725669" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11546157557653376353">It seems I'm one of the lucky few who received an advanced reader copy through a site where I signed up as a reviewer a long while ago. <br/>I picked up this novel because the blurb sounded cool and I figured I'd give the novel a shot. <br/><br/>I can summarize this book in one word: WOW!<br/><br/>Dream Caster has great potential for becoming a great series. It lacks the romance that girls these days seem to crave, but there are hints, and many hints of romance in the works between certain characters. <br/><br/>I was barely able </span>
  <span id="freeText11546157557653376353" style="display:none">It seems I'm one of the lucky few who received an advanced reader copy through a site where I signed up as a reviewer a long while ago. <br />I picked up this novel because the blurb sounded cool and I figured I'd give the novel a shot. <br /><br />I can summarize this book in one word: WOW!<br /><br />Dream Caster has great potential for becoming a great series. It lacks the romance that girls these days seem to crave, but there are hints, and many hints of romance in the works between certain characters. <br /><br />I was barely able to put this book down for a second after the first few pages got me completely hooked. <br />N.R.Nadarajah’s narrative here has immediacy to it that, when combined with the very dramatic plot is incredibly compelling. It's entertaining. If this was merely a good read, I would have given it 4 stars, but they say great art leaves you changed after you experience it... and this book definitely did that. Najeev Raj Nadarajah has, with one amazing work, propelled himself onto my top shelf. <br /><br />I can see Dream Caster joining the ranks of the hunger games, divergent, and other young adult dystopian novels. Can’t wait for book 2 !!!<br /></span>

    <a title="Andrea Korelenko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14892651-andrea-korelenko"><img alt="Andrea Korelenko" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer11266498583605072826">I almost gave this book a 3.5-4 because of the spelling.<br/>BUT WAIT. it then hit me. Canadian author, duh! lol. No wonder why certain words were spelled differently. <br/>Once I got beyond that, this book was fantastic.<br/>There were many hidden puns and word plays that (for the author's sake) I hope his readers 'get it'.<br/>A young teen might be able to read it and enjoy it, but only someone a bit older with a higher reading standard could truly appreciate it. <br/><br/>The characters and the plot was what i loved the m</span>
  <span id="freeText11266498583605072826" style="display:none">I almost gave this book a 3.5-4 because of the spelling.<br />BUT WAIT. it then hit me. Canadian author, duh! lol. No wonder why certain words were spelled differently. <br />Once I got beyond that, this book was fantastic.<br />There were many hidden puns and word plays that (for the author's sake) I hope his readers 'get it'.<br />A young teen might be able to read it and enjoy it, but only someone a bit older with a higher reading standard could truly appreciate it. <br /><br />The characters and the plot was what i loved the most. <br />Weaver, Emma-Lee and Toggen are slowly turning into a nice tandem. Toggen is just amazing lol. <br />I won't say anymore about these three, in fear of giving too much away.<br />The plot was tight. very tight. NAdarajah must've sat down and thought about the rules of our future world very thoroguhly. For an indie novel this is VERY good. It amazes me why he didn't choose the traditional route and target a publishing house.<br /><br />All in all, a highly recommended read. 5/5<br />Keep up the great work, i'm look forward to the 2nd novel</span>

<div id="review_432214354" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/432214354" />
    <a title="Suwenya Jeyarajah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13564620-suwenya-jeyarajah"><img alt="Suwenya Jeyarajah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349975413p2/13564620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/432214354?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suwenya Jeyarajah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suwenya Jeyarajah" href="/user/show/13564620-suwenya-jeyarajah">Suwenya Jeyarajah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer432214354" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2692913589975969265">What are the three most popular genres?<br/>1. Young adult<br/>2. paranormal/fantasy<br/>3. dystopian<br/><br/>Now, take all three, commercialize it, add a great story line, several pinches of moments that hint at a very, very deep backstory, a list of great characters, a lot of suspense, and a great mystery... and there we have it: Dream Caster.<br/><br/>Can someone say potential best-seller !!! <br/><br/></span>

<div id="review_478770459" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/478770459" />
    <a title="Bran Arnoldson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15529025-bran-arnoldson"><img alt="Bran Arnoldson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1355666691p2/15529025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/478770459?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bran Arnoldson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bran Arnoldson" href="/user/show/15529025-bran-arnoldson">Bran Arnoldson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer478770459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4521982021567343000">I would recommend this book to children, preteens, young adults, parents, and to all those that stay children in their hearts. <br/><br/>Some books are almost impossible to review. If a book is bad, how easily can we dwell on its flaws! But if the book is good, how do you give any recommendation that is equal the book? Unless you are an author of equal worth to the one whose work you review, what powers of prose and observation are you likely to have to fitly adorn the work? <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16077824.Dream_Caster' title='Dream Caster by Najeev Raj Nadarajah' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dream Caster</a> is at one level s</span>
  <span id="freeText4521982021567343000" style="display:none">I would recommend this book to children, preteens, young adults, parents, and to all those that stay children in their hearts. <br /><br />Some books are almost impossible to review. If a book is bad, how easily can we dwell on its flaws! But if the book is good, how do you give any recommendation that is equal the book? Unless you are an author of equal worth to the one whose work you review, what powers of prose and observation are you likely to have to fitly adorn the work? <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16077824.Dream_Caster" title="Dream Caster by Najeev Raj Nadarajah" rel="nofollow noopener">Dream Caster</a> is at one level simply a charming story, perhaps one of the most charming and most adventurous ever told by an indie author. There, see how simple that was? If you haven't read it, you should, because it is quite enjoyable. At some level, there is little more to say. Enjoy the story as the simple entertainment it was meant to be.<br /><br />But if it was only simple entertainment, I do not think that it would be anything more than just a good book. Instead, this simple young adult story resonates and fascinates. It teases and hints at something larger and grander, and it instructs and lectures as from one of the most subtle intellects without ever feeling like it is instructing, lecturing or being condescending.<br /><br />I think that is what makes this more than just a good book, but a great one. Nadarajah is able to gently skewer us for our all too human failings, and he does so without adopting any of the cynicism or self-loathing so common with those that seek out to skewer humanity for its so evident failings. <br /><br />We fantasize about heroes which are strong and comely of form, and we have for as long as we've had recorded literature. Our comic books are filled with those neo-pagan mythic heroes whose exaggerated human virtues always amount to, whatever else may be true of them, 'beats people up good'. These modern Ajaxs, Helens and Achilles dominate the box office, and I would imagine dominate our internal most private fantasy lives as well. Oh sure, the superhero of our fantasy might have superhuman ethics to go along with his superhuman ability to kick butt, attract the opposite sex, and enforce their will upon others, but it is always attached to and ultimately secondary to our fantasy of power and virility. How different is Nadarajah's protagonist from Heracles, Lancelot, Beowulf, or Batman - young, mundane, naive, and weak. Of all the principal characters of the story, he possesses probably the least of that quintessential heroic attribute - martial prowess.<br /><br />And yet, he is not actually merely an 'average Joe'. An innocent, naïve young man. Weaver is gentle. He is simple. He is humble. Power has little attraction for him. He is kind. He is a peacemaker. Though mistreated, he harbors no enmity. He never puts himself forward, but he never shirks when others do. <br /><br />How often do we fantasize about being this different sort of hero, and yet how much better we would be if we did? Some courage and some wisdom, blended in measure. How often is it that we hunger after all the wrong things? What profit would we really have if we had in great measure the power to 'beat people up good'? What real use could we put it too? How much better off would we be individually and as a people if we most desired to be graced with Weaver's virtues, rather than Achilles speed, strength, and skill with arms? How much less mature does this mere children's book of a well lit-world cause our darker fantasies to seem?<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4521982021567343000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_481289037" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/481289037" />
    <a title="Selinea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14036378-selinea"><img alt="Selinea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1355865767p2/14036378.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/481289037?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Selinea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Selinea" href="/user/show/14036378-selinea">Selinea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer481289037" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18295721200705533695">I honestly don't understand why this book is so highly rated. YA dystopian novels are a dime a dozen and even among all the riffraff, Dream Caster isn't particularly good.<br/><br/>First, the writing style, tone, and pacing itself has a tremendous amount of kinks. Rather than a coherent story building towards the end, it's a lot of exposition scenes with action scenes spliced in. And speaking of exposition, nothing in the book is introduced to the reader in an organic matter. The first half the book consi</span>
  <span id="freeText18295721200705533695" style="display:none">I honestly don't understand why this book is so highly rated. YA dystopian novels are a dime a dozen and even among all the riffraff, Dream Caster isn't particularly good.<br /><br />First, the writing style, tone, and pacing itself has a tremendous amount of kinks. Rather than a coherent story building towards the end, it's a lot of exposition scenes with action scenes spliced in. And speaking of exposition, nothing in the book is introduced to the reader in an organic matter. The first half the book consists mostly of other characters telling the main character everything he needs to know. As much as I don't like using this phrase, "show, don't tell" would be what I'd like to slap the author with. "He memorized the route using the method he developed back in his village." I'm paraphrasing because I don't feel like digging back through the book, but essentially the whole book is like that. Rather than explaining how his memory works (photographic memory is cliche, but even that would have been a better explanation than, look! The main character is a special snowflake with a mysteriously good memory that I'm not going to explain!). The author also passed off a good opportunity to really set, well, the setting. While the descriptions the author does include are decent, they are far and few in between and then entire book is way too dialogue heavy. And not good, natural flowing conversation dialogue either. It's all long explanations and somewhat pointless back and forths more for the readers benefit than for the characters themselves' benefit.<br /><br />None of the characters were particularly memorable or endearing. They function, as cogs in a wheel that move the plot along, rather than as real people to be sympathized and empathized with. The main character is one of those who's clearly <i>special</i>, one of <i>those</i> characters with a mysterious birth, backwater boy propelled into action after the village is destroyed, blah, blah. It didn't work for me in Star Wars. It didn't work for me in The Eye of the World. It didn't work for me in The Naming of the Wind. So it sure as hell isn't going to work for me in Dream Caster, a book which is flawed not just in its main character, but flawed everywhere else as well. In addition to the overdone call to action, the main character also falls into one of those "pointlessly denying the obvious", which is, of course, pointless to readers and a waste of my time to even read those pages. "There's ice formed in a warm room, but it's obviously not me, I'm obviously just a normal person." *cue eyeroll*<br /><br />I'm too seething in dislike to write coherently, but if you're a seasoned fantasy/sci-fi reader, DO NOT READ THIS BOOK. And even if you're not, The Hunger Games, Finnikin of the Rock, The Lost Years of Merlin. I guarantee whatever your book tastes, I can recommend you a book that's better than this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18295721200705533695" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_476766353" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/476766353" />
    <a title="Tracy Elizabeth Morvow" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15447809-tracy-elizabeth-morvow"><img alt="Tracy Elizabeth Morvow" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1355504576p2/15447809.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/476766353?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tracy Elizabeth Morvow" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tracy Elizabeth Morvow" href="/user/show/15447809-tracy-elizabeth-morvow">Tracy Elizabeth Morvow</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer476766353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13708076470721013816">this is offically my very first review on Good Reads<br/><br/>I found <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16077824.Dream_Caster' title='Dream Caster by Najeev Raj Nadarajah' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dream Caster</a> during a promotion on Amazon and I'm glad I downloaded it. <br/><br/>Having read a few other reviews here so far, I won't go into how great the characters were, or the beutiful imagery, the well written dialogues, the uniqueness of the genre combination and themes or anything along those lines. Instead, I'm going to talk about something entirely different. Something bold that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6552431.Najeev_Raj_Nadarajah' title='Najeev Raj Nadarajah' rel='nofollow noopener'>Najeev Raj Nadarajah</a> did in this book, which hardly anyone</span>
  <span id="freeText13708076470721013816" style="display:none">this is offically my very first review on Good Reads<br /><br />I found <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16077824.Dream_Caster" title="Dream Caster by Najeev Raj Nadarajah" rel="nofollow noopener">Dream Caster</a> during a promotion on Amazon and I'm glad I downloaded it. <br /><br />Having read a few other reviews here so far, I won't go into how great the characters were, or the beutiful imagery, the well written dialogues, the uniqueness of the genre combination and themes or anything along those lines. Instead, I'm going to talk about something entirely different. Something bold that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6552431.Najeev_Raj_Nadarajah" title="Najeev Raj Nadarajah" rel="nofollow noopener">Najeev Raj Nadarajah</a> did in this book, which hardly anyone took notice of.<br /><br />I could not help but notice the percentage of characters that were of different descent. Then again, the story is based in a post-apocalyptic Toronto. I commend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6552431.Najeev_Raj_Nadarajah" title="Najeev Raj Nadarajah" rel="nofollow noopener">Najeev Raj Nadarajah</a>for taking such a bold step and making his main characters Brown, Black, Asian, Native Canadian, etc. <br /><br />There was a time when I read a book called the city of ember and it irked me to find a post-apocalyptic world, where a few hundred people survived, and they were mostly all (with the exception of 1-2 characters) Caucasian. Don’t get me wrong, I too am Caucasian but stories like that are hard to picture and hard to believe when the author remains so narrow minded. <br /><br />Let’s try to envision this for a second. City of Ember …World ends… only Caucasian’s and a very small handful of minority survive in a country (America) with close to 200Million immigrants. Something feels wrong, doesnt it?<br />Not to make it seem like I'm beating on that one book. I'm a diehard fan of the lord of the rings. But the only coloured people in that book were all goblins, orcs, and uruk'hais. Of course, this was written in a time long ago. But we live in the present. Authors should change their way of thinking. and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6552431.Najeev_Raj_Nadarajah" title="Najeev Raj Nadarajah" rel="nofollow noopener">Najeev Raj Nadarajah</a> did!<br /><br />This is why I enjoyed reading Dream Caster, where Nadarajah painted a wonderful picture of a world that is well past its days, and laid it out through the eyes of a naive young man who was seeing the wastes of the old world for the first time. Great work on the novel. I can tell this is going to be a fantastic series, and one of immense epic proportions. I look forward to reading the rest of the series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13708076470721013816" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer409645518481498708">First of all I want to say thank you to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6552431.Najeev_Raj_Nadarajah' title='Najeev Raj Nadarajah' rel='nofollow noopener'>Najeev Raj Nadarajah</a> for gifting me a copy of <i>Dream Caster</i> thus giving me the chance to read and review your book, and wow what a book it is. What can I say it is unique, fantastic, wonderful, amazing. Those are just some of the words I could use when talking about this book. Very well written, with many h</span>
  <span id="freeText409645518481498708" style="display:none">First of all I want to say thank you to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6552431.Najeev_Raj_Nadarajah" title="Najeev Raj Nadarajah" rel="nofollow noopener">Najeev Raj Nadarajah</a> for gifting me a copy of <i>Dream Caster</i> thus giving me the chance to read and review your book, and wow what a book it is. I see big things for Najeev, and this series. I can only hope that more and more people find out about this book and this author. <br /><br />I completely loved it. What can I say it is unique, fantastic, wonderful, amazing. Those are just some of the words I could use when talking about this book. Very well written, with many humors moments, I found myself laughing out loud quite a few times. <br /><br />The characters are so likable. Naajeev has put so much thought in not just the main character but his supporting cast as well. He hasn't just written them in for the sake of doing so, they are not flat and could potentially have stories of their own to be told. Dell is definitely a favorite of mine.<br /><br /><i>Dream Caster</i> is set mainly in Toronto, Canada. Or what was once known as Toronto. It is a post apocalyptic dystopian fantasy novel. <br /><br />Please check out Najeev's <a href="http://www.nrnadarajah.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">webpage</a> if you want to learn more about the <a href="http://www.nrnadarajah.com/the-ruins-of-toronto/" rel="nofollow noopener">Ruins of Toronto</a>.<br /><br />This is a book that I can see myself re-reading again, just as I do my Harry Potter books. This series, <i>Dream Cycle</i> has so much potential and I look forward to reading the next book(s) and watching this authors career take off. I will be placing a physical copy of <i>Dream Caster</i> on my shelves in the near future. <br /><br />And I have to add one last thing, very sneaky Mr. Nadarajah, the whole second week in April line. ;) Book two, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17252254.Dreamweaver" title="Dreamweaver by Najeev Raj Nadarajah" rel="nofollow noopener">Dreamweaver</a> comes out April 9th 2013. </span>

<div id="review_473853101" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/473853101" />
    <a title="Damgaard78" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7708309-damgaard78"><img alt="Damgaard78" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/473853101?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Damgaard78" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Damgaard78" href="/user/show/7708309-damgaard78">Damgaard78</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/16077831-dream-caster">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7708309-damgaard78?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer473853101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15081134951688731069">Was offered to read the book for free if I would review it, but have no connection to the author else.<br/><br/>I devour fantasy and SF books so this book was right down my alley. It’s an interesting new take on the urban fantasy genre, which has a bit of doomsday scenario over it as well with the world having ended as we knew it. This up and coming author has a vivid imagination and it gives for a great read. It is clearly targeted for a young adult crowd, and being in the 30s myself I realized I sometim</span>
  <span id="freeText15081134951688731069" style="display:none">Was offered to read the book for free if I would review it, but have no connection to the author else.<br /><br />I devour fantasy and SF books so this book was right down my alley. It’s an interesting new take on the urban fantasy genre, which has a bit of doomsday scenario over it as well with the world having ended as we knew it. This up and coming author has a vivid imagination and it gives for a great read. It is clearly targeted for a young adult crowd, and being in the 30s myself I realized I sometimes was quite over the target. That said it is enjoyable. The protagonist is the typical orphan, growing into powers that slowly awaken as the book trundles along, but the world building and the ideas around the special powers makes it interesting, and the pages read well. <br /><br />One thing that I could have wished which I hope gets more polished in the sequel is a bit more character building. The interrelationship between the protagonist and the people he interact with goes extremely rapid, people meet and next day are tight as forever. I could have wished a bit more time had been spent on developing the relationship, might be me not understanding teenage interaction, but even I would think it takes a bit of time to get that comfortable with each other. The romantic part also seem to jump from nil to a lot more with very little interaction. That said it did not distract me more than I enjoyed the story, but this is the main reason I only gave a good story 4 stars.<br /><br />Being an ebook I can say it was very nice to be able to read a book without all the grammatical flaws that seems to be standard in so many books these days. I do not remember giving pause at any point over the grammar.<br /><br />So to sum it up, if you like YU urban fantasy I would definitely recommend giving this book a read. I will for sure check out the sequel.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15081134951688731069" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_474542703" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/474542703" />
    <a title="Joanne Corrin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15357896-joanne-corrin"><img alt="Joanne Corrin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1355162485p2/15357896.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/474542703?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joanne Corrin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joanne Corrin" href="/user/show/15357896-joanne-corrin">Joanne Corrin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer474542703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1300630770167663994">I recently met Nadarajah in a YA forum was asked to review Dream Caster as an ARC. <br/><br/><br/>It didn’t take long (perhaps 4-5 pages) before I fell in love with the style and flow of the story. The characters are truly believable and share realistic bonds (although i felt like at times their relationship could've used a bit more building). <br/><br/>There was a point in the novel when I had to stop and realize that this was only a story and these characters were only fictional. The dialogue flows very easily and con</span>
  <span id="freeText1300630770167663994" style="display:none">I recently met Nadarajah in a YA forum was asked to review Dream Caster as an ARC. <br /><br /><br />It didn’t take long (perhaps 4-5 pages) before I fell in love with the style and flow of the story. The characters are truly believable and share realistic bonds (although i felt like at times their relationship could've used a bit more building). <br /><br />There was a point in the novel when I had to stop and realize that this was only a story and these characters were only fictional. The dialogue flows very easily and conversations feel as if I was really there listening to two people speaking. There is nothing forced about it. The paragraphs are tight and there are no loose ends or plot holes. Nothing about the book was boring. It read very smoothly.<br /><br />The suspense is gradual and unbelievable. There is a cliff-hanging mystery to the novel that I enjoyed. It also makes me wonder what Nadarajah has planned for the 2nd novel in the series (Yes, there will be one). <br /><br />As for the plot, it was spectacular! Set within a post-apocalyptic world a number of years into the future, the world somehow came to an end. Fire and electricity is no more. The world as we know it is long over and even the survivors are being snuffed out one by one. And just when Weaver’s life seems to be getting on track and it seeems his future might look even a tad bit briter, hell breaks loose. Just when he gets it back under control, ALL hell breaks loose and he’s left with a nice big problem.<br /><br />I give praise to this book and feel that it’s going to go well as the series progresses. I recommend it to anyone who wants a well written story. <br />Pick it up. <br />Tell your friends. <br />Read it! </span>
  <a data-text-id="1300630770167663994" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8612228408522163031">this story is about a 16 year old boy who lives in a settlement in the future. the world is post-apocalyptic and no one knows how it came to an end. Weaver, the protagonist, lives a life where he's mistreated and kept stupid by his owner/guardian. <br/>Then just as his life begins to turn around and he gets chosen to be a Watcher of the Night, something terrible happens.<br/>He and a stranger named Abanel take off into the unknown and they come to a refuge where they are taken in. <br/>Abanel pursues her goal </span>
  <span id="freeText8612228408522163031" style="display:none">this story is about a 16 year old boy who lives in a settlement in the future. the world is post-apocalyptic and no one knows how it came to an end. Weaver, the protagonist, lives a life where he's mistreated and kept stupid by his owner/guardian. <br />Then just as his life begins to turn around and he gets chosen to be a Watcher of the Night, something terrible happens.<br />He and a stranger named Abanel take off into the unknown and they come to a refuge where they are taken in. <br />Abanel pursues her goal to be a scout and Weaver's made into a sewage and waste cleaner because he doesn't know anything else. <br /><br />Weaver is naive and slow, but he has unbelievable memory and there are subtle hints of him having greatness lurking under him. <br />He then discovers that he is a dream caster. He does not want that power or that responsibility and is in denial. but It's forced upon him. <br /><br />I can't say anymore, because you have to read the book to see how it goes. <br />Nadarajah has an odd way of writing which flows very well and sounds eloquent. The characters are loveable and hateable. The book is fast paced, funny, mysterious, and a page turner. <br /><br />It does feel like the kind of book that some will love and some will not, but either way, i think a lot of people will end up reading this book because it's only the first in the series and has a long way to go. if it's this good now, i can only imagine how much better book two can be. <br /> <br />i got this as an ARC from Nadarajah</span>

This book is one of my all-time favorites now.<br/>I haven't really been reading since school started because well my life is crazy.   <span id="freeText9644961254195596106" style="display:none">Oh. My. Holy. WOW. Amazing? Brilliant? Wonderful? All of those and more. This book is one of my all-time favorites now.<br />I haven't really been reading since school started because well my life is crazy. I have to be at school for more than 12 hours most days ....not a lot of time to read and get books from the library. But this book made me make time. I hope Nadarajah keeps the pace going and wows us with a wonderful series. <br /><br />i would also like to say i love Toggen and i love Dell and i hate Cringe. but i especially love Toggen's character...i think he's bound to be a fan favourite before the series is said and done. he almost comparable to characters like Ron from HP, Sam from LOTR, Cara from Sword of Truth, to some degree, where they're not the main characters but still, they are very thoroughly loved<br /><br />the plot starts off subtle. Weaver is naive, has no clue about anything. but there's greatness lurking within him. and then he makes a discovery, and events begin to unfold FAST. the plot is frantically paced and before you know it, the story's over and your left scratching ur heads wondering when the 2nd book will come out. <br /><br />i highly recommend Dream Caster to all fans of Young Adult Dystopian Fantasy. If this book is any indication of how great the series is going to be, i think we're in for a plesant surprise</span>

<div id="review_479822740" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/479822740" />
    <a title="Gillian Bernard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15572527-gillian-bernard"><img alt="Gillian Bernard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1355788125p2/15572527.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/479822740?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gillian Bernard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gillian Bernard" href="/user/show/15572527-gillian-bernard">Gillian Bernard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer479822740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3987747243887032548">Let me start off by saying this is one of the best Young Adult novels I have read in a very, very long time. Not only is the setting crafted expertly, but the characters are amazing, and the plot is riveting. My favorite aspect of the novel was definitely the characters. Najeev Raj Nadarajah’s ability to weave (lol) utterly believable characters (such as Weaver) is astounding. Each character had their own discernible personality, crafted through description, dialogue and their actions. Their mot</span>
  <span id="freeText3987747243887032548" style="display:none">Let me start off by saying this is one of the best Young Adult novels I have read in a very, very long time. Not only is the setting crafted expertly, but the characters are amazing, and the plot is riveting. My favorite aspect of the novel was definitely the characters. Najeev Raj Nadarajah’s ability to weave (lol) utterly believable characters (such as Weaver) is astounding. Each character had their own discernible personality, crafted through description, dialogue and their actions. Their motives for any action actually make sense, something many YA authors seem to struggle with. The connection between reader and character is incredible, especially considering the book is less than four-hundred pages. The plot is also just amazing. I was literally on the edge of my seat while reading the novel, and finished it in under one day because it was so captivating. An expertly written dystopian novel that is probably the best Young Adult novel since Harry Potter, I would recommend this to any lover of science-fiction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3987747243887032548" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer578187782" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1689491004881726001">Dream Caster, Book One of the Dream Cycle, is a young adult fantasy. Although it starts a little slow, once this story gets going, it grabs you carries you along for a wonderful journey. <br/><br/>Weaver, orphaned and under the care of a selfish man named Ruben, has only one goal, to become a guard in the small village where he's grown up.   <span id="freeText1689491004881726001" style="display:none">Dream Caster, Book One of the Dream Cycle, is a young adult fantasy. Although it starts a little slow, once this story gets going, it grabs you carries you along for a wonderful journey. <br /><br />Weaver, orphaned and under the care of a selfish man named Ruben, has only one goal, to become a guard in the small village where he's grown up. In one night, he obtains this position and in the matter of hours loses everything, his home, family and friends. <br /><br />Forced to move on as the only survival of a devastating attack of fire hounds, he soon finds a companion who travels with him to a new home. He soon discovers his true role in life, which is much bigger than he would have ever imagined.<br /><br />This well-written, intriguing story is the debut of Najeev Raj Nadarajah’s journey into the writing world. With the promise of more to this series, I predict this story teller has many more adventures to share. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1689491004881726001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Erika Manglior" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14978092-erika-manglior"><img alt="Erika Manglior" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354073495p2/14978092.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/465156854?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erika Manglior" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erika Manglior" href="/user/show/14978092-erika-manglior">Erika Manglior</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer465156854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13864521468460955458">Wow. I was barely able to put this book down for a second after the first few pages got me completely hooked. <br/>N.R.Nadarajah’s narrative here has immediacy to it that, when combined with the very dramatic plot is incredibly compelling. It's entertaining. If this was merely a good read, I would have given it 4 stars, but they say great art leaves you changed after you experience it... and this book definitely did that. Najeev Raj Nadarajah has, with one amazing work, propelled himself onto my top </span>
  <span id="freeText13864521468460955458" style="display:none">Wow. I was barely able to put this book down for a second after the first few pages got me completely hooked. <br />N.R.Nadarajah’s narrative here has immediacy to it that, when combined with the very dramatic plot is incredibly compelling. It's entertaining. If this was merely a good read, I would have given it 4 stars, but they say great art leaves you changed after you experience it... and this book definitely did that. Najeev Raj Nadarajah has, with one amazing work, propelled himself onto my top shelf. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13864521468460955458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_770447695" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/770447695" />
    <a title="Mercel Uchiha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25880568-mercel-uchiha"><img alt="Mercel Uchiha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385040403p2/25880568.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mercel Uchiha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mercel Uchiha" href="/user/show/25880568-mercel-uchiha">Mercel Uchiha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer770447695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17179274524081872407">Don't get why this book isn't popular. Needs better publicity. There's potential for big things here. <br/><br/><br/>I see enough growth left for Weaver to mature into a terrific hero by the final book. His friend Toggen is a great sidekick as well. Emma-Lee can use a little more growth, but once developed, I can see her playing an integral role in saving the world, much like what Hermione was for Harry, or Sakura for Naruto.<br/><br/><br/>Take a crack at this series. You'll enjoy it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Omn5rMf7rea1OWdwV7Hd/W8vopHCBXNROUhP5+SR/cPXZkZGLqTx3lMss5ZdLcBsJjxd8jHO50HsBMh9RmJSkA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('O8wUWo8BFAfOZ9rufVOgkPY58x+60e6T4AuT6pAtgKrWw6uwZl5IPyhyDgh3z70BvyoMfEkaeoM1RxRwMt4v+Q==')})
  }
